# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Summary of Findings

I identified **10 key C++ source files** that define the HTTP filter chain extension mechanism in Envoy v1.31.2:

### Core Components:

1. **Factory Registry** (`envoy/server/filter_config.h`):
   - `NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory` - main factory interface for HTTP filters
   - `UpstreamHttpFilterConfigFactory` - for upstream filters

2. **Filter Chain Interfaces** (`envoy/http/filter_factory.h`):
   - `FilterFactoryCb` - factory callback function typedef
   - `FilterChainFactory` - creates filter chains for new streams
   - `FilterChainManager` - manages filter registration per request
   - `FilterContext` - metadata about filters
   - `FilterChainOptions` - customization options

3. **Filter Interfaces** (`envoy/http/filter.h`):
   - `StreamDecoderFilter` - processes incoming requests
   - `StreamEncoderFilter` - processes outgoing responses
   - `StreamFilter` - combined encoder/decoder
   - `FilterChainFactoryCallbacks` - callbacks to install filters

4. **Filter Chain Execution** (`source/common/http/filter_manager.h/cc`):
   - `FilterManager` - per-request filter chain manager
   - `DownstreamFilterManager` - downstream-specific handler
   - `ActiveStreamFilterBase` - active filter wrapper with state management

5. **Configuration & Registry** (`source/common/filter/config_discovery_impl.h`):
   - `HttpFilterConfigProviderManagerImpl` - manages filter providers
   - `HttpDynamicFilterConfigProviderImpl` - ECDS dynamic configuration
   - `NamedHttpFilterFactoryCb` - pairs filter names with factories

The filter may need to handle\n60:   // watermark events when injecting a body, see:\n61:   // https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/source/docs/flow_control.md.\n62:   //\n63:   // The last call to inject data MUST have end_stream set to true to conclude the stream.\n64:   // If the filter cannot provide a body the stream should be reset.\n65:   //\n66:   // Adding a body through calling addDecodedData()/addEncodedData() then\n67:   // continueDecoding()/continueEncoding() is currently NOT supported and causes an assert failure.\n68:   //\n69:   // Adding trailers in this scenario is currently NOT supported.\n70:   //\n71:   // The filter MUST NOT attempt to continue the stream without providing a body using\n72:   // continueDecoding()/continueEncoding().\n73:   //\n74:   // TODO(yosrym93): Support adding a body in this case by calling addDecodedData()/addEncodedData()\n75:   // then continueDecoding()/continueEncoding(). To support this a new FilterManager::IterationState\n76:   // needs to be added and set when a filter returns this status in\n77:   // FilterManager::decodeHeaders/FilterManager::encodeHeaders()\n78:   // Currently, when a filter returns this, the IterationState is Continue. ContinueDecoding() MUST\n89:   // be called if continued filter iteration is desired.\n90:   //\n91:   // Used when a filter wants to stop iteration on data and trailers while waiting for headers'\n92:   // iteration to resume.\n93:   //\n94:   // If buffering the request causes buffered data to exceed the configured buffer limit, a 413 will\n95:   // be sent to the user. After request processing, response encoding follows the reverse path through encoder filters\\n\\nThe filter chain is built lazily per-request through the `FilterChainManager::applyFilterFactoryCb()` interface (line 697 in filter_manager.h), which receives FilterContext and the factory callback, allowing dynamic filter instantiation based on runtime conditions.\\n\\nThis architecture enables:\\n- **Extensibility**: New filters are added by implementing NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory and registering via the plugin system\\n- **Per-request customization**: Filters can be enabled/disabled via route-level configuration or match trees\\n- **Dynamic configuration**: Filters can be loaded dynamically via ECDS without Envoy restart\\n- **Type-safe iteration**: The ActiveStreamFilterBase system ensures filters are called in correct order with proper state management\\n\"\n}\n",
